support</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Comparison_of_layout_engines_(XHTML)" title="Comparison of layout engines (XHTML)">XHTML</a>\n<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Comparison_of_layout_engines_(XHTML_1.1)" title="Comparison of layout engines (XHTML 1.1)">1.1</a></li></ul></li></ul></td>\n</tr></tbody></table>\n<p><b>HTML5</b> is a <a href="/wiki/Markup_language" title="Markup language">markup language</a> used for structuring and presenting content on the <a href="/wiki/World_Wide_Web" title="World Wide Web">World Wide Web</a>. It is the fifth and last<sup id="cite_ref-W3C_transfer_ZDNet_3-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-W3C_transfer_ZDNet-3">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup> major <a href="/wiki/HTML" title="HTML">HTML</a> version that is a <a href="/wiki/World_Wide_Web_Consortium" title="World Wide Web Consortium">World Wide Web Consortium (W3C)</a> recommendation. The current specification is known as the <a href="/wiki/HTML#Transition_of_HTML_Publication_to_WHATWG" title="HTML">HTML Living Standard</a>. It is maintained by a consortium of the major browser vendors (<a href="/wiki/Apple_Inc." title="Apple Inc.">Apple</a>, <a href="/wiki/Google" title="Google">Google</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mozilla" title="Mozilla">Mozilla</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Microsoft" title="Microsoft">Microsoft</a>), the <a href="/wiki/Web_Hypertext_Application_Technology_Working_Group" class="mw-redirect" title="Web Hypertext Application Technology Working Group">Web Hypertext Application Technology Working Group</a> (WHATWG).\n</p><p>HTML5 was first released in a public-facing form on 22 January 2008,<sup id="cite_ref-HTML5v1_4-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-HTML5v1-4">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup> with a major update and "W3C Recommendation" status in October 2014.<sup id="cite_ref-finalars_2-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-finalars-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-5">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup> Its goals were to improve the language with support for the latest <a href="/wiki/Multimedia" title="Multimedia">multimedia</a> and other new features; to keep the language both easily readable by humans and consistently understood by computers and devices such as <a href="/wiki/Web_browser" title="Web browser">web browsers</a>, <a href="/wiki/Parsing" title="Parsing">parsers</a>, etc., without <a href="/wiki/XHTML" title="XHTML">XHTML\'s</a> rigidity; and to remain <a href="/wiki/Backward-compatible" class="mw-redirect" title="Backward-compatible">backward-compatible</a> with older software. HTML5 is intended to subsume not only <a href="/wiki/HTML_4" class="mw-redirect" title="HTML 4">HTML&#160;4</a> but also XHTML&#160;1 and <a href="/wiki/Document_Object_Model" title="Document Object Model">DOM</a> Level 2 HTML.<sup id="cite_ref-HTML5diffHTML4-quote_6-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-HTML5diffHTML4-quote-6">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>HTML5 includes detailed processing models to encourage more interoperable implementations; it extends, improves, and rationalizes the markup available for documents and introduces markup and <a href="/wiki/Application_programming_interface" class="mw-redirect" title="Application programming interface">application programming interfaces</a> (APIs) for complex <a href="/wiki/Web_application" title="Web application">web applications</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-HTML5diffHTML4_7-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-HTML5diffHTML4-7">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup> For the same reasons, HTML5 is also a candidate for cross-platform mobile applications because it includes features designed with low-powered devices in mind.\n</p><p>Many new <a href="/wiki/Syntax_(programming_languages)" title="Syntax (programming languages)">syntactic</a> features are included. To natively include and handle multimedia and <a href="/wiki/2D_computer_graphics" title="2D computer graphics">graphical</a> content, the new <a href="/wiki/HTML5_video" title="HTML5 video"><code class="nowrap" style="">&lt;video&gt;</code></a>, <a href="/wiki/HTML5_Audio" class="mw-redirect" title="HTML5 Audio"><code class="nowrap" style="">&lt;audio&gt;</code></a> and <a href="/wiki/Canvas_element" title="Canvas element"><code class="nowrap" style="">&lt;canvas&gt;</code></a> <a href="/wiki/HTML_element" title="HTML element">elements</a> were added, and support for <a href="/wiki/Scalable_vector_graphics" class="mw-redirect" title="Scalable vector graphics">scalable vector graphics</a> (SVG) content and <a href="/wiki/MathML" title="MathML">MathML</a> for mathematical formulas was also added. To enrich the <a href="/wiki/Semantic_Web" title="Semantic Web">semantic</a> content of documents, new page structure elements such as <code class="nowrap" style="">&lt;main&gt;</code>, <code class="nowrap" style="">&lt;section&gt;</code>, <a href="/wiki/Article_element_(HTML5)" class="mw-redirect" title="Article element (HTML5)"><code class="nowrap" style="">&lt;article&gt;</code></a>, <code class="nowrap" style="">&lt;header&gt;</code>, <code class="nowrap" style="">&lt;footer&gt;</code>, <code class="nowrap" style="">&lt;aside&gt;</code>, <code class="nowrap" style="">&lt;nav&gt;</code>, and <code class="nowrap" style="">&lt;figure&gt;</code> are added. New <a href="/wiki/HTML_attribute" title="HTML attribute">attributes</a> were introduced, some elements and attributes were removed, and others such as <code class="nowrap" style="">&lt;a&gt;</code>, <code class="nowrap" style="">&lt;cite&gt;</code>, and <code class="nowrap" style="">&lt;menu&gt;</code> were changed, redefined, or standardized. The APIs and <a href="/wiki/Document_Object_Model" title="Document Object Model">Document Object Model</a> (DOM) are now fundamental parts of the HTML5 specification,<sup id="cite_ref-HTML5diffHTML4_7-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-HTML5diffHTML4-7">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup> and HTML5 also better defines the processing for any invalid documents.<sup id="cite_ref-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-8">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div id="toc" class="toc" role="navigation" aria-labelledby="mw-toc-heading"><input type="checkbox" role="button" id="toctogglecheckbox" class="toctogglecheckbox" style="display:none" /><div class="toctitle" lang="en" dir="ltr"><h2 id="mw-toc-heading">Contents</h2><span class="toctogglespan"><label standards</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</li>\n</ul>\n</li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-7"><a href="#Features_and_APIs"><span class="tocnumber">2</span> <span class="toctext">Features and APIs</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-8"><a href="#Features"><span class="tocnumber">3</span> <span class="toctext">Features</span></a>\n<ul>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-9"><a href="#Markup"><span class="tocnumber">3.1</span> <span class="toctext">Markup</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-10"><a href="#New_APIs"><span class="tocnumber">3.2</span> <span class="toctext">New APIs</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-11"><a href="#XHTML_5_(XML-serialized_HTML_5)"><span class="tocnumber">3.3</span> <span class="toctext">XHTML 5 (XML-serialized HTML 5)</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-12"><a href="#Error_handling"><span class="tocnumber">3.4</span> <span class="toctext">Error handling</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-13"><a href="#Popularity"><span class="tocnumber">3.5</span> <span class="toctext">Popularity</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-14"><a href="#Differences_from_HTML_4.01_and_XHTML_1.x"><span class="tocnumber">3.6</span> <span class="toctext">Differences from HTML&#160;4.01 and XHTML&#160;1.x</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-15"><a href="#Logo"><span class="tocnumber">4</span> <span class="toctext">Logo</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-16"><a href="#Digital_rights_management"><span class="tocnumber">5</span> <span class="toctext">Digital rights management</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-17"><a href="#See_also"><span class="tocnumber">6</span> <span class="toctext">See also</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-18"><a href="#References"><span class="tocnumber">7</span> <span class="toctext">References</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-19"><a href="#External_links"><span class="tocnumber">8</span> <span class="toctext">External links</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</div>\n\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=HTML5&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: History">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<p>The <a href="/wiki/Web_Hypertext_Application_Technology_Working_Group" class="mw-redirect" title="Web Hypertext Application Technology Working Group">Web Hypertext Application Technology Working Group</a> (WHATWG) began work on the new standard in 2004. At that time, HTML&#160;4.01 had not been updated since 2000,<sup id="cite_ref-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup> and the <a href="/wiki/World_Wide_Web_Consortium" title="World Wide Web Consortium">World Wide Web Consortium</a> (W3C) was focusing future developments on <a href="/wiki/XHTML_2.0" class="mw-redirect" title="XHTML 2.0">XHTML&#160;2.0</a>. In 2009, the <a href="/wiki/W3C" class="mw-redirect" title="W3C">W3C</a> allowed the <a href="/wiki/XHTML" title="XHTML">XHTML</a> 2.0 Working Group\'s charter to expire and decided not to renew it.<sup id="cite_ref-W3C_hist_10-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-W3C_hist-10">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Mozilla_Foundation" title="Mozilla Foundation">Mozilla Foundation</a> and <a href="/wiki/Opera_Software" class="mw-redirect" title="Opera Software">Opera Software</a> presented a position paper at a World Wide Web Consortium (W3C) workshop in June 2004,<sup id="cite_ref-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup> focusing on developing technologies that are backward-compatible with existing browsers,<sup id="cite_ref-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-12">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup> including an initial draft specification of Web Forms 2.0. The workshop concluded with a vote\xe2\x80\x948 for, 14 against\xe2\x80\x94for continuing work on HTML.<sup id="cite_ref-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-13">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup> Immediately after the workshop, WHATWG was formed to start work based upon that position paper, and a second draft, Web Applications 1.0, was also announced.<sup id="cite_ref-14" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-14">&#91;14&#93;</a></sup> The two specifications were later merged to form HTML5.<sup id="cite_ref-15" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-15">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup> The HTML5 specification was adopted as the starting point of the work of the new HTML working group of the W3C in 2007.\n</p><p>WHATWG\'s <a href="/wiki/Ian_Hickson" title="Ian Hickson">Ian Hickson</a> (Google) and <a href="/wiki/Dave_Hyatt" title="Dave Hyatt">David Hyatt</a> (<a href="/wiki/Apple_Inc." title="Apple Inc.">Apple</a>) produced W3C\'s first public working draft of the specification on 22 January 2008.<sup id="cite_ref-HTML5v1_4-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-HTML5v1-4">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span id=".22Thoughts_on_Flash.22"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="&quot;Thoughts_on_Flash&quot;">"Thoughts on Flash"</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=HTML5&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: &quot;Thoughts on Flash&quot;">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Thoughts_on_Flash" title="Thoughts on Flash">Thoughts on Flash</a></div>\n<p>While some features of HTML5 are often compared to <a href="/wiki/Adobe_Flash" title="Adobe Flash">Adobe Flash</a>, the two technologies are very different. Both include features for playing audio and video within web pages, and for using <a href="/wiki/Scalable_Vector_Graphics" title="Scalable Vector Graphics">Scalable Vector Graphics</a>. However, HTML5 on its own cannot be used for animation or interactivity&#160;\xe2\x80\x93 it must be supplemented with <a href="/wiki/CSS3" class="mw-redirect" title="CSS3">CSS3</a> or <a href="/wiki/JavaScript" title="JavaScript">JavaScript</a>. There are many Flash capabilities that have no direct counterpart in HTML5 (see <a href="/wiki/Comparison_of_HTML5_and_Flash" title="Comparison of HTML5 and Flash">Comparison of HTML5 and Flash</a>). HTML5\'s interactive capabilities became a topic of mainstream media attention around April 2010<sup id="cite_ref-16" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-16">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-17" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-17">&#91;17&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-18" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-18">&#91;18&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-19" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-19">&#91;19&#93;</a></sup> after <a href="/wiki/Apple_Inc." title="Apple Inc.">Apple Inc.</a>\'s then-CEO <a href="/wiki/Steve_Jobs" title="Steve Jobs">Steve Jobs</a> issued a public letter titled "Thoughts on Flash" in which he concluded that "Flash is no longer necessary to watch video or consume any kind of web content" and that "new open standards created in the mobile era, such as HTML5, will win".<sup id="cite_ref-20" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-20">&#91;20&#93;</a></sup> This sparked a debate in web development circles suggesting that, while HTML5 provides enhanced functionality, developers must consider the varying browser support of the different parts of the standard as well as other functionality differences between HTML5 and Flash.<sup id="cite_ref-21" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-21">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup> In early November 2011, <a href="/wiki/Adobe_Inc." title="Adobe Inc.">Adobe</a> announced that it would discontinue development of Flash for mobile devices and reorient its efforts in developing tools using HTML5.<sup id="cite_ref-22" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-22">&#91;22&#93;</a></sup> On 25 July 2017, Adobe announced that both the distribution and support of Flash would cease by the end of 2020.<sup id="cite_ref-23" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-23">&#91;23&#93;</a></sup> Flash was officially discontinued on 31 December 2020 and all Flash content was blocked from running in Flash Player as of 12 January 2021.<sup id="cite_ref-24" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-24">&#91;24&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span id="Last_call.2C_candidacy.2C_and_recommendation_stages"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Last_call,_candidacy,_and_recommendation_stages">Last call, candidacy, and recommendation stages</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=HTML5&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Last call, candidacy, and recommendation stages">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>On 14 February 2011, the W3C extended the charter of its HTML Working Group with clear milestones for HTML5. In May 2011, the working group advanced HTML5 to "Last Call", an invitation to communities inside and outside W3C to confirm the technical soundness of the specification. The W3C developed a comprehensive test suite to achieve broad interoperability for the full specification by 2014, which was the target date for recommendation.<sup id="cite_ref-w3c2014_25-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-w3c2014-25">&#91;25&#93;</a></sup> In January 2011, the WHATWG renamed its "HTML5" specification <i>HTML Living Standard</i>. The W3C nevertheless continued its project to release HTML5.<sup id="cite_ref-26" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-26">&#91;26&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In July 2012, WHATWG and W3C decided on a degree of separation. W3C will continue the HTML5 specification work, focusing on a single definitive standard, which is considered as a "snapshot" by WHATWG. The WHATWG organization continues its work with HTML5 as a "living standard". The concept of a living standard is that it is never complete and is always being updated and improved. New features can be added but functionality will not be removed.<sup id="cite_ref-splits_27-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-splits-27">&#91;27&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In December 2012, W3C designated HTML5 as a Candidate Recommendation.<sup id="cite_ref-28" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-28">&#91;28&#93;</a></sup> The criterion for advancement to <a href="/wiki/World_Wide_Web_Consortium#W3C_Recommendation_(REC)" title="World Wide Web Consortium">W3C Recommendation</a> is "two 100% complete and fully interoperable implementations".<sup id="cite_ref-W3Crec_29-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-W3Crec-29">&#91;29&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>On 16 September 2014, W3C moved HTML5 to Proposed Recommendation.<sup id="cite_ref-30" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-30">&#91;30&#93;</a></sup> On 28 October 2014, HTML5 was released as a W3C Recommendation,<sup id="cite_ref-31" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-31">&#91;31&#93;</a></sup> bringing the specification process to completion.<sup id="cite_ref-finalars_2-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-finalars-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup> On 1 November 2016, HTML 5.1 was released as a W3C Recommendation.<sup id="cite_ref-32" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-32">&#91;32&#93;</a></sup> On 14 December 2017, HTML 5.2 was released as a W3C Recommendation.<sup id="cite_ref-33" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-33">&#91;33&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Timeline">Timeline</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=HTML5&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Timeline">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>The combined timelines for HTML5.0, HTML5.1 and HTML5.2:\n</p>\n<table class="wikitable">\n\n<tbody><tr>\n<th>Version</th>\n<th>First draft</th>\n<th>Candidate recommendation</th>\n<th>Recommendation\n</th></tr>\n<tr>\n<td>HTML5.0</td>\n<td>2007<sup id="cite_ref-34" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-34">&#91;34&#93;</a></sup></td>\n<td>2012</td>\n<td>2014\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td>HTML5.1</td>\n<td>2012</td>\n<td>2015</td>\n<td>2016\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td>HTML5.2<sup id="cite_ref-HTML5-201209_35-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-HTML5-201209-35">&#91;35&#93;</a></sup></td>\n<td>2015</td>\n<td>2017</td>\n<td>2017\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td>HTML5.3</td>\n<td>2017<sup id="cite_ref-5.3FWD_36-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-5.3FWD-36">&#91;36&#93;</a></sup></td>\n<td data-sort-value="" style="background: #ececec; color: #2C2C2C; vertical-align: middle; text-align: center;" class="table-na">N/A</td>\n<td data-sort-value="" style="background: #ececec; color: #2C2C2C; vertical-align: middle; text-align: center;" class="table-na">N/A\n</td></tr></tbody></table>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="W3C_and_WHATWG_conflict">W3C and WHATWG conflict</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=HTML5&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: W3C and WHATWG conflict">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/HTML#Transition_of_HTML_Publication_to_WHATWG" title="HTML">HTML \xc2\xa7&#160;Transition of HTML Publication to WHATWG</a></div>\n<p>The W3C ceded authority over the HTML and DOM standards to WHATWG on 28 May 2019, as it considered that having two standards is harmful.<sup id="cite_ref-W3C_transfer_blog_37-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-W3C_transfer_blog-37">&#91;37&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-W3C_transfer_HTML_38-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-W3C_transfer_HTML-38">&#91;38&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-W3C_transfer_memo_39-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-W3C_transfer_memo-39">&#91;39&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-W3C_transfer_ZDNet_3-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-W3C_transfer_ZDNet-3">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup> The HTML Living Standard is now authoritative. However, W3C will still participate in the development process of HTML.\n</p><p>Before the ceding of authority, W3C and WHATWG had been characterized as both working together on the development of HTML5,<sup id="cite_ref-W3C_hist_10-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-W3C_hist-10">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup> and yet also at cross purposes<sup id="cite_ref-splits_27-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-splits-27">&#91;27&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-finalars_2-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-finalars-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup> ever since the July 2012 split, creating WHATWG. The W3C standard was snapshot-based and static, while the WHATWG is a continually updated "living standard". The relationship had been described as "fragile", even a "rift",<sup id="cite_ref-tale_40-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-tale-40">&#91;40&#93;</a></sup> and characterized by "squabbling".<sup id="cite_ref-finalars_2-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-finalars-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In at least one case, namely the permissible content of the <code class="nowrap" style="">&lt;<a href="/wiki/HTML_elements#cite" class="mw-redirect" title="HTML elements">cite</a>&gt;</code> element, the two specifications directly contradicted each other (as of July&#160;2018),<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=HTML5&amp;action=edit">&#91;update&#93;</a></sup> with the W3C definition allowing a broader range of uses than the WHATWG definition.<sup id="cite_ref-41" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-41">&#91;41&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-42" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-42">&#91;42&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The "Introduction" section in the WHATWG spec (edited by <a href="/wiki/Ian_Hickson" title="Ian Hickson">Ian "Hixie" Hickson</a>) is critical of W3C, e.g. "<em>Note:</em> Although we have asked them to stop doing so, the W3C also republishes some parts of this specification as separate documents." In its "History" subsection it portrays W3C as resistant to Hickson\'s and WHATWG\'s original HTML 5 plans, then jumping on the bandwagon belatedly (though Hickson was in control of the W3C HTML 5 spec, too). Regardless, it indicates a major philosophical divide between the organizations:<sup id="cite_ref-43" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-43">&#91;43&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r996844942">.mw-parser-output .templatequote{overflow:hidden;margin:1em 0;padding:0 40px}.mw-parser-output .templatequote .templatequotecite{line-height:1.5em;text-align:left;padding-left:1.6em;margin-top:0}</style><blockquote class="templatequote"><p>For a number of years, both groups then worked together. In 2011, however, the groups came to the conclusion that they had different goals: the W3C wanted to publish a "finished" version of "HTML5", while the WHATWG wanted to continue working on a Living Standard for HTML, continuously maintaining the specification rather than freezing it in a state with known problems, and adding new features as needed to evolve the platform.</p><p>Since then, the WHATWG has been working on this specification (amongst others), and the W3C has been copying fixes made by the WHATWG into their fork of the document (which also has other changes).</p>\n</blockquote>\n<p>The two entities signed an agreement to work together on a single version of HTML on 28 May 2019.<sup id="cite_ref-44" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-44">&#91;44&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Differences_between_the_two_standards">Differences between the two standards</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=HTML5&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Differences between the two standards">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<p>In addition to the contradiction in the <code class="nowrap" style="">&lt;<a href="/wiki/HTML_elements#cite" class="mw-redirect" title="HTML elements">cite</a>&gt;</code> element mentioned above, other differences between the two standards include at least the following, as of September 2018:\n</p>\n<table href="#cite_note-:3-53">&#91;53&#93;</a></sup>).\n</td></tr></tbody></table>\n<p>The following table provides data from the Mozilla Development Network on compatibility with major browsers, as of September 2018, of HTML elements unique to one of the standards:\n</p>\n<table class="wikitable">\n<tbody><tr>\n<th>Element\n</th>\n<th>Standard\n</th>\n<th>Compatibility\n</th>\n<th>Note\n</th></tr>\n<tr>\n<td><code>&lt;rb&gt;<sup id="cite_ref-74" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-74">&#91;74&#93;</a></sup></code>\n</td>\n<td>W3C\n</td>\n<td>All browsers, except Edge\n</td>\n<td>\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td><code>&lt;rtc&gt;<sup id="cite_ref-75" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-75">&#91;75&#93;</a></sup></code>\n</td>\n<td>W3C\n</td>\n<td>None, except Firefox\n</td>\n<td>\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td><code>&lt;hgroup&gt;</code><sup id="cite_ref-76" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-76">&#91;76&#93;</a></sup>\n</td>\n<td>WHATWG\n</td>\n<td>All browsers\n</td>\n<td>"[Since] the HTML outline algorithm is not implemented in any browsers ... the <code>&lt;hgroup&gt;</code> semantics are in practice only theoretical."\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td><code>&lt;menu&gt;</code><sup id="cite_ref-77" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-77">&#91;77&#93;</a></sup>\n</td>\n<td>WHATWG\n</td>\n<td>Full support only in Edge and Firefox desktop.\n<p>Partial support in Firefox mobile.\n</p><p>Supported in Opera with user opt-in.\n</p><p>Not supported in other browsers. \n</p>\n</td>\n<td>Experimental technology\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td><code>&lt;slot&gt;<sup id="cite_ref-78" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-78">&#91;78&#93;</a></sup></code>\n</td>\n<td>WHATWG\n</td>\n<td>All browsers, except IE\n</td>\n<td>Experimental technology\n</td></tr></tbody></table>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Features_and_APIs">Features and APIs</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=HTML5&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Features and APIs">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<table class="box-Update plainlinks metadata ambox ambox-content ambox-Update" role="presentation"><tbody><tr><td class="mbox-image"><div style="width:52px"><img alt="Ambox current red.svg" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/98/Ambox_current_red.svg/42px-Ambox_current_red.svg.png" decoding="async" width="42" height="34" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/98/Ambox_current_red.svg/63px-Ambox_current_red.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/98/Ambox_current_red.svg/84px-Ambox_current_red.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="360" data-file-height="290" /></div></td><td class="mbox-text"><div class="mbox-text-span">This section needs to be <b>updated</b>. The reason given is: Last sentence marks 2016 as the future instead of past.<span class="hide-when-compact"> Please update this article to reflect recent events or newly available information.</span>  <small class="date-container"><i>(<span class="date">October 2018</span>)</i></small></div></td></tr></tbody></table>\n<p>The W3C proposed a greater reliance on modularity as a key part of the plan to make faster progress, meaning identifying specific features, either proposed or already existing in the spec, and advancing them as separate specifications. Some technologies that were originally defined in HTML 5 itself are now defined in separate specifications:\n</p>\n<ul><li>HTML Working Group&#160;\xe2\x80\x93 HTML Canvas 2D Context;</li>\n<li>Web Apps Working Group&#160;\xe2\x80\x93 <a href="/wiki/Web_Messaging" title="Web Messaging">Web Messaging</a>, <a href="/wiki/Web_worker" title="Web worker">Web workers</a>, <a href="/wiki/Web_storage" title="Web storage">Web storage</a>, <a href="/wiki/WebSocket" title="WebSocket">WebSocket</a>, <a href="/wiki/Server-sent_events" title="Server-sent events">Server-sent events</a>, <a href="/wiki/Web_Components" title="Web Components">Web Components</a><sup id="cite_ref-79" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-79">&#91;79&#93;</a></sup> (this was not part of HTML 5, though); the Web Applications Working Group was closed in October 2015 and its deliverables transferred to the Web Platform Working Group (WPWG).</li>\n<li>IETF HyBi Working Group&#160;\xe2\x80\x93 WebSocket Protocol;</li>\n<li>WebRTC Working Group&#160;\xe2\x80\x93 <a href="/wiki/WebRTC" title="WebRTC">WebRTC</a>;</li>\n<li>Web Media Text Tracks Community Group&#160;\xe2\x80\x93 <a href="/wiki/WebVTT" title="WebVTT">WebVTT</a>.</li></ul>\n<p>After the standardization of the HTML 5 specification in October 2014,<sup id="cite_ref-80" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-80">&#91;80&#93;</a></sup> the core vocabulary and features are being extended in four ways.<sup id="cite_ref-81" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-81">&#91;81&#93;</a></sup> Likewise, some features that were removed from the original HTML 5 specification have been standardized separately as modules, such as <a href="/wiki/Microdata_(HTML)" title="Microdata (HTML)">Microdata</a> and <a href="/wiki/Canvas_element" title="Canvas element">Canvas</a>. Technical specifications introduced as HTML 5 extensions such as <a href="/wiki/Polyglot_markup" title="Polyglot markup">Polyglot markup</a> have also been standardized as modules. Some W3C specifications that were originally separate specifications have been adapted as HTML 5 extensions or features, such as <a href="/wiki/Scalable_Vector_Graphics" title="Scalable Vector Graphics">SVG</a>. Some features that might have slowed down the standardization of HTML 5 were or will be standardized as upcoming specifications, instead.\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Features">Features</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=HTML5&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Features">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Markup">Markup</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=HTML5&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Markup">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>HTML 5 introduces <a href="/wiki/HTML_element" title="HTML element">elements</a> and attributes that reflect typical usage on modern websites. Some of them are semantic replacements for common uses of generic block (<code class="nowrap" style="">&lt;div&gt;</code>) and inline (<code class="nowrap" style="">&lt;span&gt;</code>) elements, for example <code class="nowrap" style="">&lt;nav&gt;</code> (website navigation block), <code class="nowrap" style="">&lt;footer&gt;</code> (usually referring to bottom of web page or to last lines of HTML code), or <code class="nowrap" style="">&lt;audio&gt;</code> and <code class="nowrap" style="">&lt;video&gt;</code> instead of <code class="nowrap" style="">&lt;object&gt;</code>.<sup id="cite_ref-82" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-82">&#91;82&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-83" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-83">&#91;83&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-84" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-84">&#91;84&#93;</a></sup>\nSome deprecated elements from <a href="/wiki/HTML_4.01" class="mw-redirect" title="HTML 4.01">HTML&#160;4.01</a> have been dropped, including purely presentational elements such as <code class="nowrap" style="">&lt;font&gt;</code> and <code class="nowrap" style="">&lt;center&gt;</code>, whose effects have long been superseded by the more capable <a href="/wiki/Cascading_Style_Sheets" class="mw-redirect" title="Cascading Style Sheets">Cascading Style Sheets</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-85" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-85">&#91;85&#93;</a></sup> There is also a renewed emphasis on the importance of client-side <a href="/wiki/JavaScript" title="JavaScript">JavaScript</a> used to create <a href="/wiki/Dynamic_web_page" title="Dynamic web page">dynamic web pages</a>.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (March 2021)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>\n</p><p>The HTML 5 syntax is no longer based on <a href="/wiki/Standard_Generalized_Markup_Language" title="Standard Generalized Markup Language">SGML</a><sup id="cite_ref-86" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-86">&#91;86&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-87" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-87">&#91;87&#93;</a></sup> despite the similarity of its markup. It has, however, been designed to be backward-compatible with common parsing of older versions of HTML. It comes with a new introductory line that looks like an SGML <a href="/wiki/Document_type_declaration" title="Document type declaration">document type declaration</a>, <code style="white-space:nowrap;">&lt;!DOCTYPE html&gt;</code>, which triggers the standards-compliant <a href="/wiki/Quirks_mode" title="Quirks mode">rendering mode</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-88" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-88">&#91;88&#93;</a></sup>\nSince 5 January 2009, HTML 5 also includes <i>Web Forms 2.0</i>, a previously separate <a href="/wiki/WHATWG" title="WHATWG">WHATWG</a> specification.<sup id="cite_ref-89" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-89">&#91;89&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-90" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-90">&#91;90&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p><br />\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="New_APIs">New APIs</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=HTML5&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: New APIs">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:422px;"><a href="/wiki/File:HTML5_APIs_and_related_technologies_taxonomy_and_status.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7f/HTML5_APIs_and_related_technologies_taxonomy_and_status.svg/420px-HTML5_APIs_and_related_technologies_taxonomy_and_status.svg.png" decoding="async" width="420" height="283" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7f/HTML5_APIs_and_related_technologies_taxonomy_and_status.svg/630px-HTML5_APIs_and_related_technologies_taxonomy_and_status.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7f/HTML5_APIs_and_related_technologies_taxonomy_and_status.svg/840px-HTML5_APIs_and_related_technologies_taxonomy_and_status.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="512" data-file-height="345" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:HTML5_APIs_and_related_technologies_taxonomy_and_status.svg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>HTML5 related APIs<sup id="cite_ref-91" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-91">&#91;91&#93;</a></sup></div></div></div>\n<p>In addition to specifying markup, HTML 5 specifies scripting <a href="/wiki/Application_programming_interfaces" class="mw-redirect" title="Application programming interfaces">application programming interfaces</a> (APIs) that can be used with <a href="/wiki/JavaScript" title="JavaScript">JavaScript</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-html4-differences_92-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-html4-differences-92">&#91;92&#93;</a></sup> Existing <a href="/wiki/Document_Object_Model" title="Document Object Model">Document Object Model</a> (DOM) interfaces are extended and <i>de facto</i> features documented. There are also new APIs, such as:\n</p>\n<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Canvas_element" title="Canvas element">Canvas</a>;<sup id="cite_ref-93" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-93">&#91;93&#93;</a></sup></li>\n<li>Timed Media Playback;<sup id="cite_ref-94" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-94">&#91;94&#93;</a></sup></li>\n<li>Offline;<sup id="cite_ref-95" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-95">&#91;95&#93;</a></sup></li>\n<li>Editable content;<sup id="cite_ref-96" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-96">&#91;96&#93;</a></sup></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Drag_and_drop" title="Drag and drop">Drag and drop</a>;<sup id="cite_ref-97" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-97">&#91;97&#93;</a></sup></li>\n<li>History;<sup id="cite_ref-98" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-98">&#91;98&#93;</a></sup></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/MIME_type" class="mw-redirect" title="MIME type">MIME type</a> and protocol handler registration;<sup id="cite_ref-99" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-99">&#91;99&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-100" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-100">&#91;100&#93;</a></sup></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Microdata_(HTML)" title="Microdata (HTML)">Microdata</a>;<sup id="cite_ref-101" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-101">&#91;101&#93;</a></sup></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Web_Messaging" title="Web Messaging">Web Messaging</a>;<sup id="cite_ref-102" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-102">&#91;102&#93;</a></sup></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Web_Storage" class="mw-redirect" title="Web Storage">Web Storage</a>&#160;\xe2\x80\x93 a key-value pair storage framework that provides behaviour similar to <a href="/wiki/HTTP_Cookie" class="mw-redirect" title="HTTP Cookie">cookies</a> but with larger storage capacity and improved API.<sup id="cite_ref-103" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-103">&#91;103&#93;</a></sup></li></ul>\n<p>Not all of the above technologies are included in the W3C HTML 5 specification, though they are in the WHATWG HTML specification.<sup id="cite_ref-104" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-104">&#91;104&#93;</a></sup> Some related technologies, which are not part of either the W3C HTML 5 or the WHATWG HTML specification, are as follows. The W3C publishes specifications for these separately:\n</p>\n<ul><li><a href="/wiki/W3C_Geolocation_API" title="W3C Geolocation API">Geolocation</a>;</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/IndexedDB" class="mw-redirect" title="IndexedDB">IndexedDB</a>&#160;\xe2\x80\x93 an indexed hierarchical key-value store (formerly WebSimpleDB);<sup id="cite_ref-105" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-105">&#91;105&#93;</a></sup></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/HTML5_File_API" title="HTML5 File API">File</a><sup id="cite_ref-106" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-106">&#91;106&#93;</a></sup>&#160;\xe2\x80\x93 an API intended to handle file uploads and file manipulation;<sup id="cite_ref-107" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-107">&#91;107&#93;</a></sup></li>\n<li>Directories and System&#160;\xe2\x80\x93 an API intended to satisfy client-side-storage use cases not well served by databases;<sup id="cite_ref-108" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-108">&#91;108&#93;</a></sup></li>\n<li>File Writer&#160;\xe2\x80\x93 an API for writing to files from web applications;<sup id="cite_ref-109" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-109">&#91;109&#93;</a></sup></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/HTML5_Audio#Web_Audio_API_and_MediaStream_Processing_API" class="mw-redirect" title="HTML5 Audio">Web Audio</a><sup id="cite_ref-110" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-110">&#91;110&#93;</a></sup>&#160;\xe2\x80\x93 a high-level JavaScript API for processing and synthesizing audio in web applications;</li>\n<li>ClassList.<sup id="cite_ref-111" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-111">&#91;111&#93;</a></sup></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Web_cryptography_API" class="mw-redirect" title="Web cryptography API">Web cryptography API</a><sup id="cite_ref-112" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-112">&#91;112&#93;</a></sup></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/WebRTC" title="WebRTC">WebRTC</a><sup id="cite_ref-113" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-113">&#91;113&#93;</a></sup></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Web_SQL_Database" title="Web SQL Database">Web SQL Database</a>&#160;\xe2\x80\x93 a local <a href="/wiki/SQL" title="SQL">SQL</a> Database (no longer maintained);<sup id="cite_ref-114" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-114">&#91;114&#93;</a></sup></li></ul>\n<p>HTML 5 cannot provide animation within web pages. Additional JavaScript or <a href="/wiki/CSS3" class="mw-redirect" title="CSS3">CSS3</a> is necessary for animating HTML elements. Animation is also possible using JavaScript and HTML 4<sup id="cite_ref-115" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-115">&#91;115&#93;</a></sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability" title="Wikipedia:Verifiability"><span title="The material near this tag failed verification of its source citation(s). (January 2011)">failed verification</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>, and within SVG elements through <a href="/wiki/Synchronized_Multimedia_Integration_Language" title="Synchronized Multimedia Integration Language">SMIL</a>, although browser support of the latter remains uneven as of 2011.\n</p>\n<h3><span id="XHTML_5_.28XML-serialized_HTML_5.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="XHTML_5_(XML-serialized_HTML_5)">XHTML 5 (XML-serialized HTML 5)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=HTML5&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: XHTML 5 (XML-serialized HTML 5)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>XML documents must be served with an XML <a href="/wiki/Internet_media_type" class="mw-redirect" title="Internet media type">Internet media type</a> (often called "<a href="/wiki/MIME" title="MIME">MIME</a> type") such as <code>application/xhtml+xml</code> or <code>application/xml</code>,<sup id="cite_ref-html4-differences_92-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-html4-differences-92">&#91;92&#93;</a></sup> and must conform to strict, well-formed syntax of XML. XHTML 5 is simply XML-serialized HTML 5 data (that is, HTML 5 constrained to XHTML\'s strict requirements, e.g., not having any unclosed tags), sent with one of XML media types. HTML that has been written to conform to both the HTML and XHTML specifications and therefore produces the same DOM tree whether parsed as HTML or XML is known as <a href="/wiki/Polyglot_markup" title="Polyglot markup">polyglot markup</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-w3c_116-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-w3c-116">&#91;116&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>There is no DTD for XHTML5.<sup id="cite_ref-117" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-117">&#91;117&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Error_handling">Error handling</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=HTML5&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Error handling">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>HTML 5 is designed so that old browsers <a href="/wiki/Forward_compatibility" title="Forward compatibility">can safely ignore</a> new HTML 5 constructs.<sup id="cite_ref-HTML5diffHTML4_7-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-HTML5diffHTML4-7">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup> In contrast to HTML 4.01, the HTML 5 specification gives detailed rules for <a href="/wiki/Lexing" class="mw-redirect" title="Lexing">lexing</a> and <a href="/wiki/Parsing" title="Parsing">parsing</a>, with the intent that compliant browsers will produce the same results when parsing incorrect syntax.<sup id="cite_ref-whatfaq_118-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-whatfaq-118">&#91;118&#93;</a></sup> Although HTML 5 now defines a consistent behavior for "<a href="/wiki/Tag_soup" title="Tag soup">tag soup</a>" documents, those documents do not conform to the HTML 5 standard.<sup id="cite_ref-whatfaq_118-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-whatfaq-118">&#91;118&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Popularity">Popularity</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=HTML5&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Popularity">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>According to a report released on 30 September 2011, 34 of the world\'s top 100 Web sites were using HTML 5&#160;&#8211;&#32;the adoption led by <a href="/wiki/Search_engine" title="Search engine">search engines</a> and <a href="/wiki/Social_network" title="Social network">social networks</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-119" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-119">&#91;119&#93;</a></sup> Another report released in August 2013 has shown that 153 of the <i><a href="/wiki/Fortune_500" title="Fortune 500">Fortune 500</a></i> U.S. companies implemented HTML5 on their corporate websites.<sup id="cite_ref-120" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-120">&#91;120&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Since 2014, HTML 5 is at least <a href="/wiki/Comparison_of_layout_engines_(HTML5)" class="mw-redirect" title="Comparison of layout engines (HTML5)">partially supported by most popular layout engines</a>.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Differences_from_HTML_4.01_and_XHTML_1.x">Differences from HTML&#160;4.01 and XHTML&#160;1.x</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=HTML5&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Differences from HTML\xc2\xa04.01 and XHTML\xc2\xa01.x">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>The following is a cursory list of differences and some specific examples.\n</p>\n<ul><li>New parsing rules: oriented towards flexible parsing and compatibility; not based on SGML</li>\n<li>Ability to use inline SVG and MathML in <code>text/html</code></li>\n<li>New <a href="/wiki/HTML_element" title="HTML element">elements</a>: <code>article</code>, <code>aside</code>, <code>audio</code>, <code>bdi</code>, <code>canvas</code>, <code>command</code>, <code>data</code>, <code>datalist</code>, <code>details</code>, <code>embed</code>, <code>figcaption</code>, <code>figure</code>, <code>footer</code>, <code>header</code>, <code>keygen</code>, <code>mark</code>, <code>meter</code>, <code>nav</code>, <code>output</code>, <code>progress</code>, <code>rp</code>, <code>rt</code>, <code><a href="/wiki/Ruby_character#HTML" title="Ruby character">ruby</a></code>, <code>section</code>, <code>source</code>, <code>summary</code>, <code>time</code>, <code>track</code>, <code>video</code>, <code>wbr</code></li>\n<li>New types of form controls: <code>dates and times</code>, <code>email</code>, <code>url</code>, <code>search</code>, <code>number</code>, <code>range</code>, <code>tel</code>, <code>color</code><sup id="cite_ref-121" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-121">&#91;121&#93;</a></sup></li>\n<li>New <a href="/wiki/HTML#Attributes" title="HTML">attributes</a>: <code>charset</code> (on <code>meta</code>), <code>async</code> (on <code>script</code>)</li>\n<li>Global attributes (that can be applied for every element): <code>id</code>, <code>tabindex</code>, <code>hidden</code>, <code>data-*</code> (custom data attributes)</li>\n<li>Deprecated elements will be dropped altogether: <code>acronym</code>, <code>applet</code>, <code>basefont</code>, <code>big</code>, <code>center</code>, <code>dir</code>, <code>font</code>, <code>frame</code>, <a href="/wiki/Framing_(World_Wide_Web)" class="mw-redirect" title="Framing (World Wide Web)"><code>frameset</code></a>, <code>isindex</code>, <code>noframes</code>, <code>strike</code>, <code>tt</code></li></ul>\n<p>W3C Working Group publishes "HTML5 differences from HTML 4",<sup id="cite_ref-122" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-122">&#91;122&#93;</a></sup> which provides a complete outline of additions, removals and changes between HTML 5 and HTML 4.\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Logo">Logo</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=HTML5&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Logo">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:122px;"><a href="/wiki/File:HTML5_logo_and_wordmark.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/61/HTML5_logo_and_wordmark.svg/120px-HTML5_logo_and_wordmark.svg.png" decoding="async" width="120" height="120" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/61/HTML5_logo_and_wordmark.svg/180px-HTML5_logo_and_wordmark.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/61/HTML5_logo_and_wordmark.svg/240px-HTML5_logo_and_wordmark.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="512" data-file-height="512" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:HTML5_logo_and_wordmark.svg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The W3C HTML5 logo</div></div></div>\n<p>On 18 January 2011, the W3C introduced a logo to represent the use of or interest in HTML 5. Unlike other badges previously issued by the W3C, it does not imply validity or conformance to a certain standard. As of 1 April 2011, this logo is official.<sup id="cite_ref-logo-faq_123-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-logo-faq-123">&#91;123&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>When initially presenting it to the public, the W3C announced the HTML 5 logo as a "general-purpose visual identity for a broad set of open web technologies, including HTML 5, <a href="/wiki/Cascading_Style_Sheets" class="mw-redirect" title="Cascading Style Sheets">CSS</a>, SVG, <a href="/wiki/Web_Open_Font_Format" title="Web Open Font Format">WOFF</a>, and others".<sup id="cite_ref-waspopenletter_124-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-waspopenletter-124">&#91;124&#93;</a></sup> Some web standard advocates, including <a href="/wiki/The_Web_Standards_Project" class="mw-redirect" title="The Web Standards Project">The Web Standards Project</a>, criticized that definition of "HTML5" as an umbrella term, pointing out the blurring of terminology and the potential for miscommunication.<sup id="cite_ref-waspopenletter_124-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-waspopenletter-124">&#91;124&#93;</a></sup> Three days later, the W3C responded to community feedback and changed the logo\'s definition, dropping the enumeration of related technologies.<sup id="cite_ref-125" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-125">&#91;125&#93;</a></sup> The W3C then said the logo "represents HTML5, the cornerstone for modern Web applications".<sup id="cite_ref-logo-faq_123-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-logo-faq-123">&#91;123&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Digital_rights_management">Digital rights management</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=HTML5&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Digital rights management">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<table class="box-Update plainlinks metadata ambox ambox-content ambox-Update" role="presentation"><tbody><tr><td class="mbox-image"><div style="width:52px"><img alt="Ambox current red.svg" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/98/Ambox_current_red.svg/42px-Ambox_current_red.svg.png" decoding="async" width="42" height="34" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/98/Ambox_current_red.svg/63px-Ambox_current_red.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/98/Ambox_current_red.svg/84px-Ambox_current_red.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="360" data-file-height="290" /></div></td><td class="mbox-text"><div class="mbox-text-span">This section needs to be <b>updated</b>. The reason given is: EME is now a W3C recommendation and thus this section seems outdated.<span class="hide-when-compact"> Please update this article to reflect recent events or newly available information.</span>  <small class="date-container"><i>(<span class="date">June 2019</span>)</i></small></div></td></tr></tbody></table>\n<p>Industry players including the <a href="/wiki/BBC" title="BBC">BBC</a>, Google, <a href="/wiki/Microsoft" title="Microsoft">Microsoft</a>, <a href="/wiki/Apple_Inc." title="Apple Inc.">Apple Inc.</a> have been lobbying for the inclusion of <a href="/wiki/Encrypted_Media_Extensions" title="Encrypted Media Extensions">Encrypted Media Extensions</a> (EME),<sup id="cite_ref-126" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-126">&#91;126&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-127" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-127">&#91;127&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-128" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-128">&#91;128&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-129" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-129">&#91;129&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-130" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-130">&#91;130&#93;</a></sup> a form of <a href="/wiki/Digital_rights_management" title="Digital rights management">digital rights management</a> (DRM), into the HTML 5 standard. As of the end of 2012 and the beginning of 2013, 27 organisations<sup id="cite_ref-131" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-131">&#91;131&#93;</a></sup> including the <a href="/wiki/Free_Software_Foundation" title="Free Software Foundation">Free Software Foundation</a><sup id="cite_ref-132" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-132">&#91;132&#93;</a></sup> have started a campaign against including digital rights management in the HTML 5 standard.<sup id="cite_ref-133" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-133">&#91;133&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-134" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-134">&#91;134&#93;</a></sup> However, in late September 2013, the W3C <a href="/wiki/HTML_Working_Group" title="HTML Working Group">HTML Working Group</a> decided that Encrypted Media Extensions, a form of DRM, was "in scope" and will potentially be included in the HTML 5.1 standard.<sup id="cite_ref-135" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-135">&#91;135&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-lowering-your-standards_136-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-lowering-your-standards-136">&#91;136&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/WHATWG" title="WHATWG">WHATWG</a>\'s "HTML Living Standard" continued to be developed without DRM-enabled proposals.<sup id="cite_ref-lowering-your-standards_136-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-lowering-your-standards-136">&#91;136&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Manu Sporny, a member of the <a href="/wiki/W3C" class="mw-redirect" title="W3C">W3C</a>, said that EME will not solve the problem it\'s supposed to address.<sup id="cite_ref-137" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-137">&#91;137&#93;</a></sup>\nOpponents point out that EME itself is just an architecture for a DRM plug-in mechanism.<sup id="cite_ref-138" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-138">&#91;138&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The initial enablers for DRM in HTML 5 were Google<sup id="cite_ref-139" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-139">&#91;139&#93;</a></sup> and Microsoft.<sup id="cite_ref-140" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-140">&#91;140&#93;</a></sup> Supporters also include Adobe.<sup id="cite_ref-141" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-141">&#91;141&#93;</a></sup> On 14 May 2014, <a href="/wiki/Mozilla_Foundation" title="Mozilla Foundation">Mozilla</a> announced plans to support EME in <a href="/wiki/Firefox" title="Firefox">Firefox</a>, the last major browser to avoid DRM.<sup id="cite_ref-gal_142-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-gal-142">&#91;142&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-baker_143-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-baker-143">&#91;143&#93;</a></sup> Calling it "a difficult and uncomfortable step", Andreas Gal of Mozilla explained that future versions of Firefox would remain open source but ship with a sandbox designed to run a content decryption module developed by Adobe,<sup id="cite_ref-gal_142-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-gal-142">&#91;142&#93;</a></sup> later it was replaced with <a href="/wiki/Widevine" title="Widevine">Widevine</a> module from <a href="/wiki/Google" title="Google">Google</a> which is much more widely adopted by content providers. While promising to "work on alternative solutions", Mozilla\'s Executive Chair <a href="/wiki/Mitchell_Baker" title="Mitchell Baker">Mitchell Baker</a> stated that a refusal to implement EME would have accomplished little more than convincing many users to switch browsers.<sup id="cite_ref-baker_143-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-baker-143">&#91;143&#93;</a></sup> This decision was condemned by <a href="/wiki/Cory_Doctorow" title="Cory Doctorow">Cory Doctorow</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Free_Software_Foundation" title="Free Software Foundation">Free Software Foundation</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-144" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-144">&#91;144&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-145" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-145">&#91;145&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="See_also">See also</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=HTML5&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: See also">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r936637989">.mw-parser-output .portal{border:solid #aaa HTML5">Cache manifest in HTML5</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Canvas_element" title="Canvas element">Canvas element</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Comparison_of_layout_engines_(HTML5)" class="mw-redirect" Introduction<span class="reference-accessdate">. Retrieved <span class="nowrap">2 March</span> 2018</span>. <q>HTML4 became a W3C Recommendation in 1997. While it continues to serve as a rough guide to many of the core features of HTML, it does not provide enough information to build implementations that interoperate with each other and, more importantly, with Web content. The same goes for XHTML1, which defines an XML serialization for HTML4, and DOM Level 2 HTML, which defines JavaScript APIs for both HTML and XHTML. HTML replaces these documents.</q></cite><span title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Ajournal&amp;rft.genre=unknown&amp;rft.jtitle=W3.org&amp;rft.atitle=HTML5+Differences+from+HTML4&amp;rft.pages=Introduction&amp;rft_id=https%3A%2F%2Fwww.w3.org%2FTR%2F2014%2FNOTE-html5-diff-20141209%2F&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AHTML5" class="Z3988"></span></span>\n</li>\n<li id="cite_note-HTML5diffHTML4-7"><span class="mw-cite-backlink">^ <a href="#cite_ref-HTML5diffHTML4_7-0"><sup><i><b>a</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-HTML5diffHTML4_7-1"><sup><i><b>b</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-HTML5diffHTML4_7-2"><sup><i><b>c</b></i></sup></a></span> <span class="reference-text"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r999302996"/><cite class="citation web cs1"><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://www.w3.org/TR/html5-diff/">"HTML5 Differences from HTML4"</a>. <i>W3.org</i>. <a href="/wiki/W3C" class="mw-redirect" title="W3C">W3C</a>. 19 October 2010<span class="reference-accessdate">.
